        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017"><meta property="og:title" content="A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi0.33Fe0.33Mn0.33O2 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/acs.langmuir.4c05017.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="O3-type layered oxide materials are regarded as optimal cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) on account of their exceptional energy density. Nevertheless, the rapid decline in capacity resulting from the instability of the interface structure represents a significant challenge to the practical implementation of these materials. In this study, we propose an innovative method to modify the O3-type NaNi0.33Fe0.33Mn0.33O2 (NFM) cathode material by applying a cross-linked polymer (CLP) coating. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis demonstrates that the CLP coating effectively inhibits the decomposition of the cathode electrolyte interface (CEI) membrane in the course of cycling, leading to a substantial improvement in the stability of the electrode material’s interface. Moreover, the oxygen-containing groups within the coating can compete with propylene carbonate (PC) solvent molecules in the electrolyte for Na+ coordination, reducing the coordination between Na+ and PC molecules. This process facilitates more efficient diffusion of Na+, thereby enhancing the rate performance. Consequently, CLP-coated NFM (NFM@CLP) materials exhibit enhanced electrochemical performance. After 300 cycles at 25 °C, NFM@CLP retains 72.36% of its capacity, compared to 62.59% for pristine NFM. Even at elevated temperatures (65 °C), the capacity retention of NFM@CLP remains high at 63.84% after 200 cycles, whereas pristine NFM drops to 3.65%. In full-cell tests (vs hard carbon), the NFM@CLP also exhibits better capacity retention (85.07% after 150 cycles). This study offers an effective and simple approach to enhancing the capacity retention and rate performance of O3-type layered materials in SIBs, providing unique insights into advanced energy storage materials."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/acs.langmuir.4c05017.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93187e228acc075b-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187e228acc075b-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '2f66622b-f944-4d18-b3e2-d4a08037b7ec'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

img{border:0}.a2a_button_facebook_like iframe{max-width:none}</style><script type="osano/blocked" async=""></script><script charset="utf-8" async="" src="https://script.hotjar.com/modules.f98993dba31a932bc912.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/requestidlecallback-polyfill-f5170b9de43ccc25622c.js"></script><script id="yui__dyn_0" type="text/javascript" src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/lazy-imports-6922fe6a4ca6b2e0cd9a.js"></script><script type="text/javascript" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187e228acc075b-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'langmuir';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/langmuir/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/langmuir/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="93187e228acc075b-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "langd5";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "A Cross-Linked Polymer Coating Strategy to Enhance the Performance of NaNi&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Fe&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;Mn&lt;sub&gt;0.33&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val">-</div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base dropBlock"><a href="#" data-db-target-for="aboutArticleMetrics" aria-describedby="about-article-metrics" class="article_aboutLink">Learn about these metrics</a><div data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/medium/la4c05017_0010.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/large/la4c05017_0010.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">O3-type layered oxide materials are regarded as optimal cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) on account of their exceptional energy density. Nevertheless, the rapid decline in capacity resulting from the instability of the interface structure represents a significant challenge to the practical implementation of these materials. In this study, we propose an innovative method to modify the O3-type NaNi<sub>0.33</sub>Fe<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.33</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NFM) cathode material by applying a cross-linked polymer (CLP) coating. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis demonstrates that the CLP coating effectively inhibits the decomposition of the cathode electrolyte interface (CEI) membrane in the course of cycling, leading to a substantial improvement in the stability of the electrode material’s interface. Moreover, the oxygen-containing groups within the coating can compete with propylene carbonate (PC) solvent molecules in the electrolyte for Na<sup>+</sup> coordination, reducing the coordination between Na<sup>+</sup> and PC molecules. This process facilitates more efficient diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>, thereby enhancing the rate performance. Consequently, CLP-coated NFM (NFM@CLP) materials exhibit enhanced electrochemical performance. After 300 cycles at 25 °C, NFM@CLP retains 72.36% of its capacity, compared to 62.59% for pristine NFM. Even at elevated temperatures (65 °C), the capacity retention of NFM@CLP remains high at 63.84% after 200 cycles, whereas pristine NFM drops to 3.65%. In full-cell tests (vs hard carbon), the NFM@CLP also exhibits better capacity retention (85.07% after 150 cycles). This study offers an effective and simple approach to enhancing the capacity retention and rate performance of O3-type layered materials in SIBs, providing unique insights into advanced energy storage materials.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D4296%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYixuan%2BBai%252C%2BXin%2BWang%252C%2BAli%2BShamshad%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D41%26issueNum%3D6%26contentID%3Dacs.langmuir.4c05017%26title%3DA%2BCross-Linked%2BPolymer%2BCoating%2BStrategy%2Bto%2BEnhance%2Bthe%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BNaNi0.33Fe0.33Mn0.33O2%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D0743-7463%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dlangd5%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D4306%26publicationDate%3DFebruary%2B2025" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2025 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291557&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Coating materials"> Coating materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292120&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrolytes"> Electrolytes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291675&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Stability"> Stability </a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The accelerated global expansion of renewable energy sources has underscored the critical importance of efficient and cost-effective energy conversion devices. Against this backdrop, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have garnered significant attention for their distinctive advantages. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> The abundance and ease of extraction of sodium from seawater and rock salt, in comparison to lithium, make it a highly sustainable resource for the extensive deployment of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4 ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 3 to 5">(3−5)</a> Nevertheless, despite these advantages, SIBs still encounter obstacles pertaining to reduced energy density and diminished cycle stability when contrasted with lithium-ion batteries (LIBs). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 6 and 7">(6,7)</a> Consequently, the development of electrode materials for SIBs that demonstrate high capacity, rate performance, and exemplary cycle stability has become a pivotal domain of research.</div><div class="NLM_p">In recent years, research on cathode materials for SIBs has explored a range of different types, including layered oxides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 8 to 11">(8−11)</a> polyanionic compounds, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> Prussian blue analogs, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 13 and 14">(13,14)</a> and organic compounds. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> Of these, O3-type layered oxides (Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TMO<sub>2</sub>, 0.8 &lt; <i>x</i> ≤ 1; TM = Ni, Fe, Mn, Cr, Co, V, Cu, or their mixtures) have attracted significant attention due to their high theoretical capacity, suitable operating potential, and simple synthesis process. Nevertheless, O3-type layered oxides still encounter several obstacles in practical implementation. One significant challenge is structural instability resulting from multiphase transitions, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> which impairs the reversible capacity and cycle stability of layered oxides. Furthermore, during cycling in the electrolyte, layered oxides may undergo a series of interfacial side reactions, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> including electrolyte decomposition under high voltage, which triggers HF attacks and leads to irreversible dissolution of transition metals and gas release. These processes significantly compromise the stability of the electrode material and reduce the battery’s lifespan.</div><div class="NLM_p">To overcome these challenges, researchers have put forth a proposal to enhance material stability by regulating both the bulk and interface structures. The regulation of the bulk structure typically involves the introduction of dopants, such as copper, magnesium, titanium, and other elements. Jung et al. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> found that Mg doping effectively inhibits irreversible structural degradation and induces more reversible phase transitions. The optimized NaMg<sub>0.05</sub>[Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>]<sub>0.95</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exhibits superior cycle stability, retaining 77% of its capacity after 50 cycles, in comparison to 40% for the undoped NaNFM. The primary method for regulating the interface structure is through the use of surface coating techniques. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18,19)</a> Hwang et al. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> successfully coated dense nanoscale Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> particles on the surface of an O3-type NaNi<sub>0.6</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> through the ball-milling process. The Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> layer effectively reduces parasitic reactions between the electrode material and the electrolyte solution, facilitating Na<sup>+</sup> migration and significantly enhancing the cycle stability and rate performance. Turgeman et al. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> employed atomic layer deposition (ALD) to uniformly coat lithium/sodium-aluminate on the surface of Ni<sub>0.230</sub>Co<sub>0.115</sub>Mn<sub>0.513</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathodes, thereby creating a passivation layer that prevents oxygen loss and electrolyte decomposition, thus enhancing the surface stability. Despite the advantages offered by an inorganic coating, there are several challenges associated with its use. These include high costs, which often necessitate secondary annealing processes, as well as the potential for the coating layer to become detached and for the coating to be uneven. Furthermore, ALD presents significant financial challenges and intricate procedural requirements. Fortunately, organic wet-chemical coating technology provides a more cost-effective solution to these issues.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Cross-linked polymers (CLPs) are a widely used material in polymer electrolyte membranes (PEMs) in solid-state LIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> They offer significant potential in the battery field due to their remarkable thermal stability, interfacial compatibility, cycling stability, and high safety. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22 ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 22 to 24">(22−24)</a> This research explores the potential of CLPs to enhance the performance of SIBs as cathode materials. A novel approach was employed whereby CLP coatings were applied to the NaNi<sub>0.33</sub>Fe<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.33</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode materials via a straightforward wet-chemical method, resulting in a functional coating layer. The coating layer serves as an efficient physical barrier, effectively preventing a straight contact between cathode materials and electrolyte and protecting the cathode electrolyte interface (CEI) membrane during battery cycling, thereby significantly enhancing the cyclic stability of the battery. Furthermore, the CLP coating reduces the coordination between solvent molecules propylene carbonate (PC) and Na<sup>+</sup>. This optimizes the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion efficiency of the electrode materials, consequently enhancing the rate capability of the battery. This strategy offers a unique method for optimizing the electrochemical performance of the SIB cathode, contributing to the advancement of energy storage technology.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Methods</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Synthesis of NaNi<sub>0.33</sub>Fe<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.33</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (NFM) Cathode</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The requisite quantities of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, NiO, Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, and MnO<sub>2</sub> were measured with precision based on the established stoichiometric ratios and then subjected to wet ball milling at 350 rpm for 12 h. An excess of 2 mol % Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> was employed to offset any potential volatilization of Na during the calcination process. Subsequently, the precursors were calcined for 15 h at 900 °C (5 °C min<sup>–1</sup>) in a KSL-1100X-S muffle furnace. The calcined samples were stored in a vacuum desiccator.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Synthesis of NFM@CLP</h3><div class="NLM_p">To further enhance the stability of the NFM material, a wet-chemical method was employed to coat its surface with a CLP film (as illustrated in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme 1</a>). Initially, a binary mixture of PEGDA (poly(ethylene glycol) diacrylate) as the cross-linker and PEGMEA (poly(ethylene glycol) methyl ether methacrylate) as the monomer was prepared in a 1:4 weight ratio within an argon-filled glovebox. Subsequently, acetone was added to the PEGDA/PEGMEA blend, resulting in solution A. Under light-shielded conditions, 2 wt % of the photoinitiator UV819 (phenylbis (2, 4, 6-trimethylbenzoyl) phosphine oxide) was incorporated into 4 g of acetone, yielding solution B. Thereafter, varying quantities of solution A were introduced to three sets of solution B, each containing 1 g of bare NFM material. Following thorough mixing, all solutions were simultaneously subjected to uniform ultraviolet (UV) irradiation at 350 nm for 15 min. Subsequently, the samples were subjected to centrifugation and subsequent drying at 60 °C in a vacuum oven. The samples were labeled NFM@CLP1, NFM@CLP2, and NFM@CLP3 and stored in a vacuum desiccator.</div><figure id="sch1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/medium/la4c05017_0009.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/large/la4c05017_0009.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Illustration of the Wet-Chemical Coating Process for the Fabrication of the NaNi<sub>0.33</sub>Fe<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.33</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Coated with CLP Material</div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017/asset/images/large/la4c05017_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c05017&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Material Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The crystal structure of the samples was examined by utilizing the X-ray diffraction (XRD) instrument, specifically the Rigaku MiniFlex 600 model. XRD measurements were performed with Cu Kα radiation (λ = 1.5406 Å) at 40 kV and 15 mA, with a scanning speed of 10° per minute. The chemical composition of the prepared sample was analyzed by an inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometry (ICP-OES, PerkinElmer Avio 500) instrument. Additionally, the coating content was calculated using a thermogravimetric analyzer (TGA, NETZSCH STA449C) at a ramp rate of 10 °C min<sup>–1</sup>, under an airflow of 20 mL min<sup>–1</sup>. The surface morphology and properties were examined by using a scanning electron microscope (SEM, Phenom Pharos). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) analyses were performed on a Talos F200X electron microscope at 200 kV. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) measurements were conducted in macro mode using an Escalab Xi+ instrument. Raman spectroscopy measurements were performed by using a HORIBA XploRA PLUS system with a 532 nm laser, with each spectrum representing an average of 10 scans. The samples for analysis were prepared within a glovebox and sealed in glass tubes for subsequent analysis.</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Electrochemical Test</h3><div class="NLM_p">The cathode electrode preparation process entailed the mixing of cathode materials (NFM, NFM@CLP1, NFM@CLP2, and NFM@CLP3), Super-P, and poly(vinylidene fluoride) (8:1:1) in <i>N</i>-methylpyrolidinone to form a homogeneous slurry. The slurry was uniformly coated onto aluminum foil and dried in a vacuum oven at 80 °C for 12 h. The dried electrode was then punched into 12 mm diameter disks with an average active material loading of 3–4 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. The electrodes were stored in an argon-filled glovebox prior to use.</div><div class="NLM_p last">For electrochemical evaluation, half-cells were assembled using CR2032 button cells with a glass fiber separator, gasket, and spring spacer. Sodium metal was used as both the counter and reference electrodes in the half-cell configuration. In full-cell tests, hard carbon was employed as the anode with a negative-to-positive-capacity (N/P) ratio of 1.1. Furthermore, a solution of 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in a PC/EMC (1:1 volume ratio with 4.0% FEC) was employed as the electrolyte (130 μL for the half-cell and 400 μL for the full-cell). Galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) tests were performed on a Neware CT-4000 workstation within a voltage range of 2.0–4.0 V to evaluate cycling stability and rate capability. Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements were also conducted on the same workstation, where cells were charged at 26 mA g<sup>–1</sup> (0.2C) for 10 min, followed by a 3 h relaxation period. To streamline the calculation process, the effective surface area (<i>S</i>) and molecular volume (<i>V</i><sub>m</sub>) were assumed to be 1 for all samples. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were conducted by using the CHI 760E electrochemical workstation from Chenhua Instruments. Additionally, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was performed on the same workstation, with a frequency range spanning from 0.01 to 100,000 Hz and an applied amplitude of 5 mV.</div></div><div id="sec2_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i9" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i9"> Density Functional Theory (DFT) Calculations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">To comprehend the molecular interactions within electrolytes, we conducted DFT calculations utilizing the ORCA 5.0.4 software package. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 25 and 26">(25,26)</a> The geometric configurations of all molecules and ions were refined using the B3LYP-D3 <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> density functional in conjunction with the def2-TZVP(-f) basis set. Subsequently, the single-point energies of these optimized structures were determined using the PWPB95-D3 <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> density functional and the def2-TZVPP <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> basis set. For the sake of simplicity, the polymer CLP was represented by diethylene glycol monoethyl ether acetate and the SMD <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> continuum solvation model was employed to calculate the single-point energies in the electrolyte environment. The molecular geometries were visualized through the use of VMD <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> and Multiwfn <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 32 and 33">(32,33)</a> software tools. The definition of the binding energy (<i>E</i><sub>b</sub>) existing between Na<sup>+</sup> and the solvent is<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview"
